% This file is based on the new high-resolution Berkeley Earth global temperature
% data set.  It expands upon the previous Berkeley Earth temperature data set by
% including predictive structures based on historical weather patterns and 
% increasing the underlying resolution to 0.25° x 0.25° latitude-longitude.
% Files based on this new data set are being provided as part of an early preview
% to aid in the identification of any remaining bugs or errors.  While, we 
% believe the current dataset to be accurate and useful, it is still in 
% development and substantial revisions remain possible if significant issues
% are identified.
% 
% LOCAL AND REGIONAL UNCERTAINTIES ARE STILL BEING UPDATED AND NOT YET REPORTED.
% 
%%%%%%%
% 
% This file contains an extracted regional summary of land-surface 
% temperature results produced by the high-resolution Berkeley Earth averaging 
% method for the region: 
% 
%    Cyprus No Mans Area
% 
% The Berkeley Earth method takes temperature observations from a large 
% collection of weather monitoring stations and produces an estimate of 
% the underlying global temperature field across all of the Earth's 
% land areas.  Once this temperature field has been generated, it is 
% possible to estimate the temperature evolution of individual regions 
% simply by integrating the field over the region in question.  This 
% file contains such a regional estimate.
% 
% For references and more information about the methods employed,
% please refer to the global average files and/of the Berkeley Earth
% website, http://berkeleyearth.org/
% 
% Temperatures are in Celsius and reported as anomalies relative to the 
% Jan 1951-Dec 1980 average.  Uncertainties represent the 95% confidence 
% interval for statistical noise and spatial undersampling effects.  Such 
% uncertainties are expected to account for the effects of random 
% noise as well as random biases affecting station trends and random 
% shifts in station baselines.  The analysis framework is expected to be 
% robust against most forms of bias; however, the impact of some forms of 
% possible systematic bias is still being studied.
% 
% The current dataset presented here is described as: 
% 
%   Land_TAVG_Monthly
% 
% 
% This analysis was run on 17-Sep-2025 00:52:42
% 
% Global results are based on 56751 time series 
%   with 23088806 monthly data points
% 
% The current region is characterized by: 
%%   Name: Cyprus No Mans Area
%%   Latitude Range: 34.98 to 35.19
%%   Longitude Range: 32.58 to 34.02
%%   Area: 366.63 km^2
%%   Percent of global land area: 0.000 %
%%   Approximate number of temperature stations: 1
%%   Approximate number of monthly observations: 255
% 
% Note that all results reported here are derived from the full field 
% analysis and will in general include information from many additional 
% stations that border the current region and not just those that lie 
% within this region.  In general, the temperature anomaly field has 
% significant correlations extending over greater than 1000 km, which 
% allows even distant stations to provide some insight at times when 
% local coverage may be lacking. 
% 
%%  Estimated Jan 1951-Dec 1980 absolute temperature (C): 18.51 +/-  NaN
% 
% Estimated Jan 1951-Dec 1980 monthly absolute temperature (C):
%       Jan    Feb    Mar    Apr    May    Jun    Jul    Aug    Sep    Oct    Nov    Dec

%%  +/-    NaN    NaN    NaN    NaN    NaN    NaN    NaN    NaN    NaN    NaN    NaN    NaN
% 
% For each month, we report the estimated land-surface anomaly for that 
% month and its uncertainty.  We also report the corresponding values for 
% year, five-year, ten-year, and twenty-year moving averages CENTERED about 
% that month (rounding down if the center is in between months).  For example, 
% the annual average from January to December 1950 is reported at June 1950. 
% 
% Annual averages are explicit 12-month moving averages.  Five, ten, and twenty
% year averages use a LOESS style regression (rather than a uniform averqage)
% in order to produce smoother trends, free from short-term noise.
% 
% Values are reported as missing (i.e. NaN) when station coverage within 
% the region becomes too low, even though a limited number of observations may

% be reported as long as at least 75% of the necessary values are available.
